## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of concentration dA/dt as a function of time t and concentration A. In chemical kinetics, rate laws typically express dA/dt as functions of concentration (power laws, rational forms), with possible explicit time dependence for non-autonomous systems.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to square of concentration)
- n-th order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (combination of first and second order)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme-catalyzed or saturation kinetics)
- Langmuir-Hinshelwood: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)**2 (surface reaction kinetics)
- Autocatalytic with decay: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 + c2 * A) (autocatalytic reaction)
- Time-dependent first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-varying rate constant)
- Reversible reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (first-order with back reaction at equilibrium)
- Competitive inhibition: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A + c2 * A**2) (substrate inhibition kinetics)
- Power-law with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (fractional order with constant source/sink)
- Time-modulated rate: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + t) (rate decreasing with catalyst deactivation)
- Sigmoidal kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (Hill-type cooperative kinetics)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Negative rate values (consumption) with magnitude increasing with A → simple power-law rate dA_dt = -c * A^n with n > 0
- Rate approaching zero as A approaches zero → rate law must vanish at A=0, suggesting multiplicative A dependence
- Rate leveling off at high concentrations → saturation kinetics with rational fraction A/(c+A) structure
- Rate showing a maximum at intermediate A → autocatalytic or substrate-inhibition mechanism with A*(c1 - c2*A) or A/(c+A)^2
- Explicit time dependence in rate → catalyst deactivation, photochemical forcing, or intermediate species eliminated via quasi-steady-state
- Log-linear relationship between log|dA_dt| and log(A) → power-law kinetics with slope giving reaction order
- Rate proportional to product A*(A0-A) → reversible or autocatalytic reaction where A0 is initial concentration encoded as constant
- Rate changing sign at a specific concentration → equilibrium point indicating reversible reaction with dA_dt = c0*(A - c1)
